O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, my dear children, I have completed this book which is the accumulation of medical knowledge and its conclusions through explanations and statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come to me that I shall complete this treatise with the subject of surgery (which comes from "the work of hands").
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the hands are skilled in our region and can perform every task without difficulty, surgery is practiced everywhere, and there's no delay from performing small operations as described by ancient texts that have been executed by these hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because of this arises both mistake and pride, opinions are closed off, and the practice of medicine is distanced from them.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation;	I seem to bring it back together in accordance with the instructions of this treatment following the path of exposure and announcement, and abbreviation.
et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	And I shall bring together the forms of fire cupping and other utensils for this craft with the adjustment and preparation of these tools as necessary; thus it is left to the expertise of the practitioner.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no such master in hands is found among us, the art of healing extends beyond our reach.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And they who venture into this shall strive in the science of anatomy as Galen says, grasping firmly the judgment of bones and forms—and connections; understanding the structures of bone and nerves, movement when active or at rest, their number, shape, arrangement, position within a socket —knowledge essential for healing.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc;	And because Ibrac is who says it with them [the instruments], and with blood.
et meismement en l’art de main.	and immediately in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes;	We tell you in the beginning of this book that anyone who is not considering what has been previously stated will make mistakes and offend people.
ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	I have often desired many others who intermingle in this art and abandon themselves to its practice without sense or experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col;	I see a mad eye that pours over an abscess and pokes the blood vessels at the neck.
por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For moisture so much blood is out, it's as if a dead woman’s flesh lies between her hands.

si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	If it carries away part of the bladder, and becomes mort within three years.

pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois;	Take a root of aristogollium as long as you can find it and let it dry out or keep it large and long like you must.
et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe;	and apply oil to the moisture, and grasp with fire, and perform cautery between the fingers and beard area, and small burns a little in the part under the mustache.
et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc;	And between the fifth rib and the sixth, with a little push downward.
et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules;	And with the fire cautery on my leg, and another above my stomach, and between these two spaces are the other joints of this leg which move freely under the influence of the same cautery that is between these two spaces.
et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	And do not squeeze your hand, but make an open cut as when smelling something fragrant.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme;	And no ancient spoke of anyone using fire cupping as if it were tailors' pincers, and they remove them and place between the ribs until it arrives at that spot.
et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And it jumps forward like we said in the abdominal examination.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear among patients who have died or an abscess that cannot be made healthy.

de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Fire cautery does not hold value on its own, except as applied with "ascltyes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis;	When you treat according to the methods we have discussed in sections, and your treatment does not benefit at all yet, it will be that you must make four cauterizations inside (likely referring to different parts of the body), two underneath the stomach, one beneath the liver, another below the intestines ('mice' might refer historically to a term for small digestive organs or possibly misinterpreted anatomy here), and two along the spine; furthermore, make four cauterizations at this spot (possibly indicating pain or injury location) on the belly.
et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	And let the cautery instruments well placed on the sharp edge of the knife.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere;	After applying the cautery leave it open for bleeding to continue long enough, and do not abandon any further treatment of the patient afterward.
et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	and healing would hasten, and they will come together as two entities with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit;	And the form of the cauterization for the abdomen should be such that our previous demonstration showed it to us;  
et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	And if it is about its back being olive (referring to skin coloration), according as that which has been placed there before.
de l’enfleure des piez	from the inflammation of pressure,
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire;	When the joints are swollen due to inflammation and have a yellowish hue, it is necessary that you perform an incision on their back between the ring finger and little finger.
et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	and apply your hand with the cauterizing instrument to turn around.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deep into them where the yellowish hue is so severe, and shape your cauterizing instrument accordingly.
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire;	After performing two cauterizations in one leg at the tip of the toenail;
et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe;	and shape them such that one is on the front side and another moves away down the leg. et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	And if they have such or similar issues wherein their flesh is of different colors and so forth; with regard to the socketed joint's bone as well colored.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil;	In those cases of such jointed limbs which are not discolored or marred, it is necessary for the patient to position themselves between their hands towards the sun.
et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers;	And work their nostrubs (nostrils), and drain those limbs' fluids;  
pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Cause you to hold tightly under the small handle of a reflex hammer on one side, as long as you know that the joint is entirely bony.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien;	And if it remains no part whatsoever not to cover up, and the small handle of the reflex hammer touches lightly on all its joints without holding anything back.
et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient;	and if not clad with clothes or cauterized as it requires.
et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	and if they are incurably ill with the wound being dressed or cauterized as needed; then apply quick and hot wine or vinegar to all parts of one's body until he is relieved from pain and inflammation.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez;	If he enters firework without protection, it comes just to his palace (body), where he is safe.
et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier:	and if they penetrate as he intends, it enters into the bone below (skull), where his brain comes up for cutting; that is not through any means of sawing down here.

puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement;	Then bind the wide nervous bandage until his tongue is out of place, and if it hardens or knots up, indicating a fracture wound, tighten that binding firmly.
et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz;	and make sure the wound is not too deeply penetrated by arteries.
et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin;	and once done, if you have a warm ointment or cold one (warm and cool), apply it with a swab of linen.

puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	Then continue with other treatments until he is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre;	and if you see the flesh black or dark brown as it is hardened, but they do not feel pain, there is no need to touch at all, for this indicates ulceration.
et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre;	If he is leaning towards collapse and has wetness within him, if he cries out in pain, then take a gentle splint, provide relief from both sides.

des apostemes de la gorge	Of the throat incisions
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde:	Never comes from the throat with barked breaths called "godath," and they are properly treated on the two almonds; when you treat them, as we have said in discussion, if not sound, then take care.
se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	If it is a hard abscess with dark flesh and consistency, do not attempt to touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc;	And if it is red and the root is large, do not attempt to touch with iron, either for the bleeding.
mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi;	But leave it until dead, and then you will remove it; otherwise, it would break itself apart.
et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	and be made of either silver or refined iron like a knife:

et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And no other stones in the throat shall grow than these two almonds; for they too bear chains.

et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II. li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille;	Moisture causes dislocations, as this memory comes after from one and other in this book, varying into piercing and cutting.
et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	And it is by these two methods; one being similar to itself, and of that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method involves placing them on the joints.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	Because the application of force at the head is different from that on the base, and the method for dealing with ligaments differs from those in natural joints; each person must form their judgment regarding it all within the artwork (craft).
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement;	And if at an application of force there is no piercing involved, as long as the bow remains dead in accordance with its fulfillment.
et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there is such that it must be pierced when present; and they do not die according to their fulfillment, just like the ones applied in proximity of joints (implying treatment).
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	When abscesses come from the joinings and it is left there while it's red hot, possibly because the ligament and nerve of the joint have been corrupted; hence, this causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil;	Where the main bone is located underneath it, and if you delay piercing until it's dead, harm will befall on the principal bone.
ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs;	Where lies its foundation, should one pierce as if it were already dead;  
et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule;	And they should not only pierce the abscess crust with sensory knowledge completed for digestion but also ensure that whoever is near the base does not perforate it and become inflamed.
et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	and cannot heal in a great length of time.

et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	and if it takes a little while, and he doesn't complain about the wound of any corrosive powders used for treatment, tightens the wound, applying soothing things at once with gentle heat. The patient is cured until they are healthy again;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	and if it hurts greatly, when he licks the two lips of the wound and his tongue is affected by these actions;

puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	Then return to the bed where it lingers.

et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And these are necessary for their joints.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The chief of these are cutting tools and those who cut only one way will scrape us, so that they won't touch the vein or nerve.

et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif;	and if it is not healthy, or the incision has been made in vain because patients cannot rest, or to stop bleeding as necessary, then you must fill the wound with lint soaked in a caustic dressing..

de la routure de l’artere	from the rouging of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme;	When the blood vessel is open, and the skin above it hardened as well, often times many flee from or pierce through.

dou chancre	The sore lesion
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer;	We have observed the resemblance of ulcers and how one should act with remedies, as well as addressing iron treatment.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called for treatment, and I thought about it longingly but could not sew the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed under strong pressure of magnetism, and there from it came an ossicle, then others followed after some days.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I vomited blood because the belly had no bones inside.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	Thinking it was bones of a dead child.

et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu;	And left her long in this way, adding a little arrow of lead hereafter. pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large;	Take I threaded wire, and drive it into a needle, then wind the thread on top of the needle's shaft, piercing the other end with it. Turn the two ends of the thread around the point of the needle, if they are wide enough;
et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc;	And tighten the thread formed, then wind it back onto the needle, and remove the pinching instrument (the aguille), doing so for all others as well. Leave to drain any remaining blood in this way too;  
puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose;	Then lay it upon the foundation with a wax or wooden pincet, and place it on the foundation, and command the patient to rest.
et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then leave it until they are healed, and if other treatments for wounds are needed while they remain healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	gently on the foundation or joints
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times are found blood in the intestines, and due to natural restraints, and when the illness is old and medicine no longer has value.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir;	If you find that it must be reset at the hinge or on your elbow bone's outer shell, which does not allow to become wet.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient;	Then treat as long as he is soaked if it seems necessary.
et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez;	And if he cannot dry out, should the cautery begin again more vigorously until he recovers fully and be scalded.
puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat as long as he is healthy.
dou fremit	and trembles faintly, indicating a weak or fe

Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor;	And the treatment is such that you take a cane made of goose quill or strong hawk feather and place it under the swelling until the purple circles around there are completely inflamed.
puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	Turn your hand to all parts of the joint until you feel its movement within the sinews and push it into place again.

des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies;	We have said in dividing the treatment of wounds;
or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	Or you shall say the treatments for hands and medicine according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various depending on what they consist of and according to their nature; from where it is made up until here lies the cause for them being created.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made include the grinding of stones, and sizes of spearheads and axes, or arrows from bows and crossbows, lances and firearm barrel pieces (like muskets), siege equipment such as trebuchets, catapult balls ("siettes"), etc.

Sore wounds come from cuts or injuries; they are simple if there is no difference between the affected part and its counterpart, but when the limb or blood vessel has been severed.

Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres;	and herein they intend to administer care as it has appeared in my hand. Here the text instructs using gentle manipulation with one's hands and assembling of lips for addressing small wounds, indicating an approach that involves delicate handling possibly aimed at healing or preparation for treatment without further trauma.
et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort;	and that is the common way of suturing (stitching), and it may involve using either one or more needles, depending on the size of the wound's gap. Here they specify how to proceed with closing large gaps in a wound: firstly by stitching together what remains open as much space is filled; secondly where needed use strong suture material for reinforcement—this denotes an approach tailored according to specific circumstances and requirements of the injury being treated, following age-old medical practices.
et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble;	Cut the two pieces of silk with the two chisels, which are inside the skin, until you pierce through that part and assemble the four pairs together.
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	Then draw out one thread of the needle with two parts, and join together the two ends of the wound dressing, leave one inch space, and then fix another needle.
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	Then take the thread if you have made the first needle, and continue to do so according to what you are skilled in with needles, until all the wound is contained.
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	And be they small or large droplets, for the fine ones seep through all of it and the larger cannot penetrate well enough.
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	for them to remain moist;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	and do not thrust the needles too deep into the flesh and leather where they cut or rub the wound before the seam.
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and then straighten the needles, so they do not pierce through the patient while sleeping, and set them in tents or cloth for thorns to hold the needle ends together until the wound is healed.
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II.	And this method of suturing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it suffices one or two stitches.
Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien;	The second method of suturing is common and involves assembling two pieces of leather with one piece of strong thread using the needle.
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	And when you have perceived all these four pieces assembled, if the needle enters where you began threading them in this manner. (Note: This sentence is somewhat ambiguous and seems to refer back to an earlier instruction on what steps to take after assembly or initial stitching.)
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	And place a small piece of leather between some sutures. (This sentence suggests that the practitioner should use an additional strip or pad, possibly for padding around a wound to aid in healing.)
ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	This seam lies on the seventh side of their home, and I stitched a wound where one had an abdomen wounded by a knife; it was more than an arm's length large, with intestines protruding two hands wide into its depth.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I pulled the intestine out then; it was healed after forty-four hours and sanitized over fifteen days of care.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they believed his eyes would die, and this was a miracle.
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	and did not care for him with ointment because in my land or here there was no remedy found.
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	and apply more than once a day to the wound, using cold water and honey as long as it is healed.

et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	And we understand this dressing method as the carpenter does with nails and leaves it for one side, then repairs on the other until the whole is complete. Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	The second way of cautery that Galen prescribes properly, so much like no other craftsmen who assemble the two parts together naturally and apply one headpiece to another in such manner.
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac;	Insert a needle or small hook for the next joint, and pierce it through gently, leaving both ends of the sinew.
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac;	Then turn the needle, and make a piercing through those parts down to its ends, at these two joints of the shoulder.
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	Then pierce one and another of those parts down to its ends, in two more joints that are located on the other side.
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is how it's commonly done for mending.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	If the patient does not understand this language and has no witness to testify, one must sew with needles in two places, using thread for each.

The "young" intestine cannot heal when it is filled with feces, and this relates to the plants of worms that are within them, as well as the delicacy of the entire body's flesh and how closely its nature aligns with nerves.

Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens;	And I hastened forthwith and wound around one of the branches until I found a part of bone within it, which was decayed or rotten inside, coming from the bone itself. This reveals an early form of medical diagnosis where examining parts of dislocated joints for signs of damage could indicate further intervention required to address underlying issues such as infection due to exposed and possibly decomposing tissue within a fracture or injury site.
je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai;	I observed that which appeared to me from the bone decayed, and took care it would not undergo any other deterioration than what I was observing.
et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder;	and made efforts to restore the wound with salves for an extended period, but could not seal it shut.
et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu;	and then I renewed the effort and discovered the bone as if beforehand, finding continuous decay within it, which I treated and continued to tend until I was able to sew up the wound.
mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines;	but I could not mend it fully so I took hold of an olive branch from the bone and applied treatments as much to its entirety then restored it with remedies.
et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	and it was healed and sewn swiftly, and they did not wish to continue the work of this remedy for fear that the patient would suffer any further harm from their weakness or because I feared death at his behest.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurs, but he was entirely cured and in his flesh grew hard bone, which had no harm to all or any part therein nor affected it on arrival or coming up.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere:	And if the bone of the limb is fractured in any way, he must be treated as follows:
pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut;	Prepare it herein, and stretch at the head of the bone that has opened, and command no one to extend upwards.
et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char;	And tie another piece of wool more substantial than the first one around the shank that is above the bone, and position it where you see suede underneath, to prevent the cloth from wetting the bone.
et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue;	And place coal or a small torch on top of the bone to cover up decay.
et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	and will surely showcase such contamination as we can see and feel it, and at times again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute;	And if the bone is decayed and does not open itself, and rotations are within or in a segment where it can be detected throughout its extent; uncover all of it.
puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit;	Then place kindling on it, and cover the part from one another decay, let its covering be as long as we have said.
et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part;	And the rot is in the joint, if it covers the impademalled union of bone from another portion; and cover the os within that.
et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper;	And the rot is in either one or both unions connecting them, if there's no other covering than kindling on top of it.
et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert;	And if the rot is in a finger or toe joint, but it must be that you enclose the decay therein as directed how. (Note: The last line seems to imply an action of containing or addressing the presence of corrosion/rot within a body part such as a hand or foot.)
et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire;	and purify it in all ways you can, but do not interfere with the vein or nerve.
et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce;	And where the incisors and hairs cover these bones many times over, according to their position on the bone's surface, as well as thickness and delicacy, size and fragility, hardness.
et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument;	And therefore they must appear different versions of their tools for each situation.
et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies;	And they show that the instrument will shape your tool according to your mastery of this craft and witnessing how these diseases are managed.
si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If you use it in accordance with what it requires from you.
dou feu	by fire, indicating the next step
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;	The head is dislocated either due to pressure within or because of exposure to flame. This sentence describes two possible causes for a joint being forced out of place – one resulting from internal force
et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre;	And when you have medicine for the curing of these diseases and they do not benefit at all, cover that limb until wherever this cure comes into contact, if then those patients risk death or mischance greater than error in the member.
et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors;	And if the signs show that the limb turns black, as though it were charred by fire, and afterward becomes covered with rust on body parts, take oil all over the skin.
si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	Hurry not to close it, and if through the percussion of any venomous creatures such as scorpions or snakes, so that like a sea creature's sting and worm bite, corruption is at its head, even then do not hasten with your hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;	And if it comes to the arm through touching or closing, even then does not the decay show itself in arms alone.
et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute;	And if she comes to the arm, then take it by the wrist.
et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut;	and if you pull on the wrist, that's it—the arm is broken, and there are no further remedies than what her vitality allows.
et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet:	And as long as there is rust or iron filings here.
s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe;	When it comes to the first joint, if after the other joint;
et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet;	And if she comes or falls down, she covers all of her fall.
et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil;	and if she rises on the leg, it touches at the knee joint;  
et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort;	And if it comes above the knee joint, there is no other instrument for the patient than gentle stretching.
et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers;	And the method of covering or padding the limb so that it is above and below, stretching bands one atop the other downward towards the ankle (I tibia), extending others upwards along the thigh bone until the bone becomes exposed.
puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Then apply wax or silk, and place some strips of linen so that the fabric does not touch the healthy joint, but covers other injuries and abrasions.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans;	And when blood comes as you work, if you cauterize the joint quickly, or place any constricting powders thereon.
puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the painful limb with such cord that can be untied and heal as long as it remains healthy.
et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet:	And I will tell you what happened to me at my house in peace. (Note: This sentence appears incomplete or out of context with the preceding lines, so it's translated literally without additional commentary

et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	But that's all I know except for what we have made here before.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe;	Never comes the time to reset a dislocated limb in haste, and it takes so much effort that many arrows are drawn. 
et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz;	And they go forth and pierce him with their bow, drawing his limp feet as if he were a squire. 
et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»;	And the skin above is so subtle as to be likened to fine linen, and will not harm bone or muscle, nor such disease that it either calls itself "healing" or refers to "canker".
mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»;	but if it is so long that it pierces through to the bone at its endpoints, then they call it "fistula.

Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi:	And if you have wedding bands that chafe and the decay is not yet at its end, and the skin becomes as hard as hide, then with this treatment of an enema today:
regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite:	Look at how big it is, and the boar that comes from within; soon you will administer to him the Egyptian medical cleansing potion here described.

et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez;	and never is an alkali of ashes used when this medicine is prescribed, and you should first pour ash from the grape vine into water above, then strain it down, and in a cleansing act likewise continue until you are certain that their breasts are well moistened.
et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet;	and if the patients cannot endure it, nor does Egyptian medication employ ashes of saltwater, unless there is an application of strong alkali water with honey or a touch of quicksilver infused.

et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez;	And it is small at the breast and cannot be cleansed with a poultice that I have described their properties for balms; if an iron spoon expands it slightly enough, or Egyptian ointment, or basilicatum wax paste, as long as they enlarge.

And if the wound is too wide for cleansing or poultice to enter, and when it lies above where arrows are shot (which could indicate a location on the body like an arm), even so long as the sword's point or anything lower than that can reach.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char;	For when arrows are in flight, it does not allow them to be restrained by charm. (Here 'charm' may refer metaphorically to healing or protection spells.)
et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere:	and if you cannot cover the breast as when you see it, so that the bowstring touches its lowest point there, for whenever the bowstring is drawn, neither moisture nor discomfort remain.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the incision on a nail

When you treat it as we have described in the division, and if the remedy does not benefit at all, then remove any excess that remains on the skin afterward, and then apply cautery to the wound afterwards.

et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout;	After the joint is displaced and begins to swell, ensure you apply pressure on the affected joint so that no further movement occurs from it. et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if you see the bone disrupted or broken as described, then treat it until healthy again. The translation provided reflects a medieval medical approach to treating displaced joints and injuries with ointments while emphasizing gentle handling of affected areas for proper healing without causing further harm.

Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet;	Those who are unable to move at all on either side do not recover, and those who have affected the junction of both sides may become immobile due to chance.
la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere:	The size of a heavy person is done so lightly thus.

Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere:	The size if thus:
arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil;	The limb arises as such: lift the leg by a hot steam strong enough so that the thick skin is not disturbed until it reaches below the knee, where you then stretch the affected limb downwards from above the ankle.

Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere:	The application of it follows this manner:

de la voinne civile	of a civilian vessel (note that in historical medical texts, "la
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This civilian vessel is formed by legs with no grass or tree growths and without dampness.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Of those that grow between hide and flesh.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	This disease is prevalent in our land as the "cattle sickness," because it often arises from beasts and is a small worm that exists between hide and flesh. It moves throughout the body of cattle upward and downward by their joints, affecting each limb with its presence until reaching either skin or bone where it continues to move rapidly;

des saiettes	of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their shapes and by means of which they pierce skin or flesh.

et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	And thoroughly applied it for three months and then sharpened the tools on both sides as needed, but could not extract them.
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	adonques never ceased to refine and engage in techniques of handling the tools, as long as I had my sharp nails made up properly according to how it will be at the end of this chapter, so long as I treat it and kept the wound closed.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And he deems that the nasal septum cannot restore itself.
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	and I will repair it here and now, and the wound shall be healed, and my patient entirely cleansed of illness.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	You have stated the quality of extracting any arrows that you cannot disclose to me because books can only grasp so much.
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	But your masters are most proficient in this craft and what is currently therein presented; the removal of things drawn out through this practice takes nine o'clock effort with a new tool, to dissect those external entities involved herein.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres:	I declare that arrows do not come from any joint, unless according to two methods.
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or through the flesh where they enter, or by another means;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	and that which jumps into the flesh is a shard entering in the body's meat and no longer does so now;
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn'thy not now, let her stay as long as the flesh rots or swells from its injury.

Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide:	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and goes towards one of the chambers of the brain, among the misfortunes I have mentioned to the patient:
si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if you do not remove it, but leave it as long as it remains stationary after any seasons, for the arrow comes by itself through a fissure, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not come by itself through a fissure, nor causes pain or harm over any seasons without attempts to remove it, death will befall when someone tries to extract it as an accidental injury.

de la brisure de l’espaule	from the fracture of the shoulder blade
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement;	Whenever the shoulder breaks or widens its joints, it moves within itself, and they are only displaced by touch.

Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the application of linen and warmth to the ligaments, mending them as well; this is similar in kind when necessary for the patient.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if warmth cannot come to the northern extremity of it, because it is too easterly, then you must soften that part with a poultice; and leave such days on so long as the cold returns, and then apply pressure.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things come to the patient within XX days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos;	Or if none of these things come to the patient within XX days. Then bind their hands at their neck and keep them still without motion or turning on top of their backs;
et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	and how long this dislocation is restored in X years or in XV days, and perhaps within Y years, according to the compositions and constitutions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of hand fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Whenever there are breaks on our hands or fingers, only falls occur many times over.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement;	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bent, if they must also grasp it straightly as well;
puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint;	Then places his hand on the extended sleeve and extends their bones outwardly until they are properly joined.
et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu;	And applies plaster and pincers when they don't come together naturally, then he sets a pin according to the quantity of lead.
et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie;	And if the break is in its core due to wind within the plant, make a linen sheet and command the patient that they stretch it across their broken part of the body.
et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	Then the strain of a long linen bandage is applied, and so should be its tightness like that found in the bones of the hand; thus it must be adjusted accordingly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in a jointed position, you must place one pin above it and another on its plantar surface; thus your hand should be overturned and straightened out before being completely bound together with these pins between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient;	And if it breaks at any of our joints that are affected, should we apply pressure to make sure.
et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve;	and if it breaks and the plant is used for support with a small stick to lift the fracture, let it not move.
et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés;	and if the break is among those joints or in either of them, should we apply pressure and use our healthy limb that follows.
ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet;	or you can hold all together with your hand, which makes sense or by using a stick if necessary for any of them.
et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	and apply warmth in the restoration and positioning of hot abscesses, and secure what comes forth as I have stated.
de la cuixe brisie	Of a broken joint
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier;	The bone of the shoulder is often fractured, which one can see when it turns forward and backward.
et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	And if there lies between the breakage above (the scapula), then this is where he lays it down again; and that other part must be dealt with accordingly.

Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus;	If bone fractures are present and you observe these broken pieces moving against each other, as if they were stones on the earth or in flight like a bird taking off, then place your finger under them. Lift carefully until straightened positions arise for their return to normal state; apply pressure continuously so long that it restores what belongs within itself (i.e., aligns and stabilizes). This line is guiding someone on how to manage bone fractures by manually repositioning the displaced pieces, suggesting they hold them in place while applying steady force until proper alignment or healing occurs naturally under pressure—a rudimentary form of setting a broken limb before any modern medical intervention.

This line of treatment from medieval times indicates a careful approach towards immobilization, aiming not to move too much but just enough so that bone fragments may realign with each other—a precursor understanding in the management of fractures before modern orthopedic care techniques were developed.

(Here "esteit" likely refers to a kind of bandage or dressing used at that time.)

(Here "coverture" refers to a form of dressing or wrapping used for injuries.)

et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And let the strains be more moisture and sharp than other fractures.

Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener;	And you must reset it so that joints become immobile in clothing and fabric as they come into contact with these materials. puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	then lay it down, and let him lie comfortably until his limbs are comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	from the shoulder joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres:	The joints are dislocated according to three methods:
c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier;	That is said by means of pushing inwards and forwards, and backwards.
et ne desalue point devant.	and not forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And if you command the patient to bend their leg at the knee, and it does not straighten out there, then it is dislocated. To translate this instruction accurately into modern English understanding: If a person instructs someone with an injury (the "malaide") to attempt to flex or bend their injured leg at the knee joint—and if that movement doesn't naturally restore full extension of the limb, then it suggests dislocation. The language used here is reminiscent of Old French medical terminology
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And if you make the patient sit down straight and extend their leg—if they can do it themselves —and position your back under his face, and place him on your knees. To translate this line into contemporary English instructions: Have the injured person assume a seated posture with an upright back beneath them; then assist in extending or supporting that same limb if possible while you provide support using your own knees—this could be part of stabilizing and assessing their injury for potential treatment.
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment;	Then take your thigh with your palms, and draw back between your knees, then fold the two sides of the thigh.
et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	And other ministers extend their finger, so long as the joint returns to its place, and it shows that he bends his leg well at the knee.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie;	Put on the splint for the leg at the knee, and bind them together firmly for three or four days, then remove it.
et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Do not make the patients move until their limbs are supported.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the members are not in place, so that forceful extension is applied as we have described for treating a hinge joint until it becomes healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of a dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The ankles are never properly touched or healed entirely; they suffer from pain and fall off inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And signs show that the leg is displaced, with attempts made to realign it at the point where it has been dislodged.
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And if ligament damage is present, and he must extend the injured limb using his hands when touched gently. Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when he is being dislodged entirely from the limb, it's necessary to make sure that you place the patient upright and use spinal supports above their knee joint. The translation reflects direct instructions for handling a case of complete ligamentous rupture or similar injury as per medieval medical protocol without additional commentary on historical accuracy or linguistic nuances beyond straightforward English rendering from Old French to modern language.
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	Then grasp it with your right hand, and then with the left twice, hold it up high, and let the shoulder joint stay in the upper position.
et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet;	And do this twice as we have instructed, thrusting and pulling upon his flesh.
s’elle revient, c’est bien;	If it returns, that's good enough.
se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	But if it starts again, because it comes back;
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	If it cannot return there, then have the patient lay on their back on the ground, and firmly press a stick between their joints, so that they do not sweat.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then you spread your fingers or extend the palm of hand on it, as if underneath the skin. 
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then all must extend evenly, and the patient's limbs should be positioned between the joints of the doctor to hold the patient when they are being stretched.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then place ice on the displaced joint and another minister bends the healthy leg; thus, the dislocation returns quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is firmly set in place, they apply the splint and bind up above, securing both legs to prevent too much extension towards their heel. In this way, no ligaments are overstressed.
puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain;	Then they leave it for two or three days and loosen the bindings if necessary stiffness occurs. The specificity of these instructions reflects an understanding that treatment may require adjustments over time as healing progresses. This line emphasizes a caut
puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors;	Then lift it up during the day or by a quarter, and definitely guide the patient over four years.
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And if he goes ahead before that time is up, there's no way to secure him anymore.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it comes into the air or breaths we mentioned elsewhere, there is a need for you to calm it down until he is sound again.
des dois	Should calibrate and adjust accordingly
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the joints are being worked on again, if they present themselves as extended or strained there'll be work to do; it is a light task nonetheless.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocation is not caused by pressure on the back or spine, there's need to make him sit with his leg up against your knee (or lap) and press firmly until he returns.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie;	And when it is immobile and has not opened at all, place the plant of pepper on two points of its joints, then form them tightly, leave for three days, then dissolve.
et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let him rest until he is healthy again.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When injury comes with dislocation, it is often necessary to restore her; many times patients die.
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	If you are not careful in the treatment, and if you lack skill or do not practice it for a long time, and if you are neither compassionate nor merciful, and late arrivals, don't be bold.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	Use at first gentle heat applications with warmth applied externally and let the patient hold onto it unless there is hope for healing.
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, if now reset the limb back into place, so that the external warmth applications may fade away.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is back in place, if necessary apply calming applications with external warmth and treat any wounds as it seems fitting, using dew-dried ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And in cases of severe breakage along with the dislocation, and if bones are involved, do as we have done for simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	Keep from entering the path of fear as I have described, for it is according to your Maker that you act and by virtue of wisdom in arms and body armor.
